Free Talk

To Our Contributors (Editor) 101

Dear Contributors:

We would like to discuss with you the future direction of improvement for this publication. Before addressing this topic, we would like to express our sincere gratitude. In the past, this publication has been overly anticipated by readers, and this is the result of your love for this publication and your efforts to assist us. However, in our opinion, to adapt to modern society and the needs of new readers, this publication must also find ways to transform and slightly improve its past direction. Therefore, we have decided to strictly regulate the submission guidelines starting from September 1st, and to open a new path for this publication. We hope that you will make practical efforts to help this publication truly achieve its "improvement" goals, and to make it more interesting and sympathetic to the general reader. This is our wish.

The following are the newly revised submission guidelines:

(1) Submissions must be short stories rich in modernity, such as realistic portrayals of society, family and women's lives, interesting science talks, youth cultivation, miscellaneous thoughts, and casual conversations.

(2) Submissions must be lively in writing, thorough in understanding, sincere in emotion, and rich in humor. Submissions with outdated ideas or stale facts will not be accepted.

(3) In addition to the title, add a subtitle of one or two sentences, but it must be very novel and eye-catching.

(4) The word count for each article is strictly limited to 500 words. Please indicate the word count at the end of the manuscript.

(5) Submissions can be in classical or vernacular Chinese, but must use new punctuation. Emphasize key phrases and words by enclosing them in circles.

(6) This publication welcomes short essays of 100-200 words that are profound and alerting or humorous and interesting, as well as slogan-like short sentences of 30-50 words.

(7) Increase in manuscript fees, with standard remuneration based on quality rather than quantity.

The Soul of the Nation 102

— Qian Taisheng

The three provinces of the Northeast, mired in deep water and intense heat, are, to put it sadly, nearing their "anniversary." Hundreds of thousands of brave soldiers in the Northeast are hoping that the inland will quickly send a large army to recover the lost territory. How eagerly do these brave soldiers, a mixture of iron and blood, await the revival of their motherland? When the sorghum fields rise, they take advantage of the situation to attack the enemy troops everywhere, causing chaos and disarray among the enemy forces. They swallowed the treasure of the three Northeast provinces in one gulp, but they never thought that in the depths of those mountains and forests, there would be a group of brave soldiers who do not cry out in pain when injured, and who are not afraid to rush forward and die, constantly inflicting heavy blows on the enemy troops and achieving surprising victories everywhere. The dwarfs, upon hearing the sound of the old northeast wind and the old gang leaders, are so frightened that they lose their courage and souls. They thought they had seized the treasure of the three Northeast provinces, but they never thought it was a fierce bomb buried deep inside!

In July, this group of Northeast soldiers, who were rolling in blood and sand, according to the enemy's own transmission, attacked in various places a total of 1,036 times. We can imagine that each time, in that pitch-black night, the soldiers crawling in the sorghum fields, upon seeing the enemy, disregard their own lives and charge towards the enemy. Head falling, arm breaking, they really disregard it, and even if the entire army is wiped out, it is only to earn the enemy's triumphant sneer: the clash of bullets and flesh and blood bursts out the soul of the inherent nation for thousands of years!

General Ma Zhanshan, the new national hero, did indeed wait silently for a year, and the brave soldiers in the deep mountains and forests of various places also remotely led the large army in the inland with concern. Do you really think that the soul of this nation, this group of agile northeastern soldiers like rabbits, that the enemy's sharp weapons, the iron birds flying in the air, and the 250-pound bombs, really cannot conquer this group of brave soldiers with exhausted ammunition and few guns?

With the "anniversary" of the Northeast fast approaching, who should this responsibility be placed on?

Interpretation of Suzhou Proverbs 103

— Farmer Fanning Cattle

▲戚子卿篤小二弗説好話盲詞小説雙金錠。中有揚州王三小姐來蘇告狀。至城中因果巷投奔著名訟師吴縣生員戚子卿。畫僮小二官胡言亂語一段明代故事。考長洲諸人矱野獲編。德清俞曲園茶香室叢鈔。皆載戚子卿確有其人。家住因果巷頗富有。築讀書樓。題額曰鴛鴦。繞屋遍種梅花。在四通橋右云云。清乾隆長洲進士顧俠君（嗣立）秀野草堂。一名五百梅花草堂。在閭邱坊。閭邱坊與因果巷後巷前巷。明末清初。顧氏秀野梅花。或即戚氏鴛鴦梅花。雙金錠小説。謂王三小姐認戚子卿作母舅。大成坊口寫狀伸寃。戚子卿窮無聊赖。酸氣撲鼻。與褚俞所記。全乎不合。惟戚子卿篇小二官弗説好詞之諺。悉從雙金錠説都中來。小二官爲子卿之齎值。無錫産。蘇州人謂家曰篤。係俗字。

"Qi Ziqing and the Dumb Boy Never Say Nice Things" is a proverb mentioned in the blind storyteller's novel *Double Gold Ingots*. The story involves Miss Wang San from Yangzhou coming to Suzhou to file a lawsuit. She seeks refuge with the famous lawyer Qi Ziqing, a scholar from Wu County, in Yinguo Lane in the city. The painting servant Xiaoguan's nonsensical ramblings are a story from the Ming Dynasty. According to *Records Gleaned from the Wild* by people from Changzhou and *Tea Fragrance Studio Miscellany* by Yu Quyuan of Deqing, Qi Ziqing was a real person. He lived in Yinguo Lane and was quite wealthy. He built a study and named it Mandarin Duck, planting plum blossoms all around the house, located to the right of the Sitong Bridge. Gu Xiajun (Silin), a jinshi from Changzhou during the Qing Dynasty under the Qianlong Emperor, owned Xiuye Thatched Cottage, also known as the Five Hundred Plum Blossom Cottage, in Luqiu Fang. Luqiu Fang and Yinguo Lane were located behind and in front of each other. During the late Ming and early Qing Dynasties, Gu's Xiuye plum blossoms might have been Qi's Mandarin Duck plum blossoms. The *Double Gold Ingots* novel states that Miss Wang San recognized Qi Ziqing as her maternal uncle, and wrote a complaint at the entrance of Dacheng Fang to seek justice. Qi Ziqing was described as poor, bored, and with a strong sour smell, which is completely inconsistent with the records of Chu and Yu. However, the proverb "Xiaoguan of the Qi Ziqing chapter never says nice things" in the *Double Gold Ingots* all comes from the capital. Xiaoguan was Qi Ziqing's servant. Homes in Wuxi were called "Du" by the people of Suzhou, which is a colloquial term.

▲走盡三關六碼頭孟子。古之爲關也。將以禦暴。今之爲關也。將以爲暴。春秋戰國時己然。何况後世。蘇州乃闔閭舊都。吴宫花草。譽美東南。緑水青山。艶稱今古。城周圍三十六里。旱門八。水門八。上應八風。下應八卦。伍子胥督造。設備周至。他處城池皆不及焉。原有三關六碼頭。百貨雲屯。萬商霧集。所以有金閶銀胥。銅齊鐵葑之稱。三關則一爲滸墅關。一爲鐵嶺關。一爲鷄鳴關。今關址猶存。六碼頭。則一爲萬人碼頭。誤犯人碼頭。前清外府六十三州縣遞解民刑重囚進省。赴臬憲衙門聽審。必須由水路船隻來。在萬人碼頭登岸。由是訛傅作犯人。一爲接官廳碼頭在胥門萬年橋。凡官員上任由他處來。必在此登岸。故曰接官碼頭。其餘四碼頭。詢諸白髮老翁。亦瞠目無以對。

"Walk Through the Three Passes and Six Docks" Mencius said, "In ancient times, the purpose of passes was to defend against violence. Today, the purpose of passes is to perpetrate violence." This was already the case during the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods, let alone later generations. Suzhou was the old capital of Helu. The flowers and plants of the Wu Palace are praised as beautiful in the southeast. The green waters and green mountains are praised as beautiful in ancient and modern times. The city is thirty-six miles around, with eight dry gates and eight water gates, corresponding to the eight winds and eight trigrams. Wu Zixu supervised the construction, and the facilities were comprehensive. Other cities could not compare. Originally, there were three passes and six docks, with all kinds of goods gathered and merchants gathered like clouds. Hence, there was the saying "Golden Chang Gate, Silver Xu Gate, Copper Qi Gate, Iron Feng Gate." One of the three passes was the Hushu Pass, one was the Tieling Pass, and one was the Jiming Pass. The sites of the passes still exist today. One of the six docks was the Wanren Dock, mistakenly referred to as the Prisoner Dock. During the Qing Dynasty, the sixty-three prefectures and counties of the outer provinces escorted civil and criminal heavy prisoners to the province for trial at the Niexian Yamen. They had to arrive by waterway and disembark at the Wanren Dock. Hence, the rumor that it was the Prisoner Dock. One was the Jieguanting Dock at the Wannian Bridge in the Xu Gate. All officials who took office from other places had to disembark here, hence the name Jieguan Dock. When asked about the remaining four docks, even the old men with white hair stared blankly and could not answer.

The Strange and Tragic Cholera Epidemic in Neijiang 104

— Zizai

The widespread and rapid spread of the cholera epidemic this year is unprecedented in recent times. According to the areas affected by the epidemic announced by the Department of Health, it has reached fifteen provinces, including Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Hebei, Shandong, Henan, Shaanxi, Suiyuan, Fujian, Guangdong, Chahar, and Sichuan. The extent of the spread cannot be said to be narrow. Yesterday, Yunbing came from western Sichuan and disembarked at Xingteng Wharf. He talked about the recent situation of the cholera epidemic in Neijiang, Sichuan. Its rampant and tragic nature is truly terrifying. I am recording it on the left to assist the discussion.

Due to abnormal weather, a cholera epidemic broke out in Neijiang. In twenty days, more than 3,000 people died. The Wang Xueyuan Regiment, which was transferred from Longchang to Neijiang, arrived at the end of July. Within three days, more than ninety people died, so they moved to another village to avoid it. Currently, the county seat is experiencing a shortage of coffins due to the large number of deaths. Many people use bed boards to convert coffins. Most of the dead are poor. Some wrap corpses in cotton blankets or straw mats for soft burials. Some use large wooden boxes to carry the corpses of children. Many families have been completely wiped out. Someone named Liu asked a friend in a teahouse, "How many corpses were carried out of Zhongjie this morning?" The friend replied, "Sixty-four corpses." While Liu was talking and laughing, he suddenly collapsed and lost consciousness. His friend initially thought it was a joke, but when he saw his face change color, he sought medical treatment. Before the doctor arrived, Liu had already died. Also, the Taoist Zhao Longwen went to Longyuan to perform rituals. Three people died in A's family, two in B's family, and one in C's family. When the Taoist was performing rituals in B's house, he fell to the ground and could not get up. The owner thought he was performing rituals. After a long time, they called him but he did not respond. He was breathless and his body was cold. There was also a traditional Chinese medicine practitioner named Yang Zhihou. He diagnosed six people with the epidemic in someone's home. Before the diagnosis was completed and the prescription was written, the doctor said, "I will surely die after I go home.

Random Thoughts 105

— Zhu

The Northeast has fallen for a year now. The honorable officials are still clinging to the dream of a fragmented peace, relying solely on the volunteer army organized by remnants of outlaws, fighting in the white waters and black mountains, using their flesh and blood against the enemy's aircraft and heavy artillery,

fighting for the final victory. They bathe in blood and fight fiercely, falling one after another. Such commendable and tearful deeds are met with sighs of sorrow and generous donations from all those with a sense of justice and patriotism, to show their sincere sympathy and shared hatred for the enemy. However, the banking sector in our Suzhou area has not a single bank that assists in collecting donations for the Northeast Volunteer Army, as if they were strangers from Qin and Yue, indifferent and unrelated. Since the September 18th Incident, Suzhou's banking sector has never donated more than a hundred yuan. Only when the 19th Route Army retreated to the second line of defense and Japanese aircraft frequently came to inspect, did they urgently request the authorities to dismantle the fire watchtower to avoid attracting the attention of Japanese aircraft. "We are not responsible for the country's demise." Unexpectedly, the bankers of Suzhou also share the ambition of great men. How admirable!

The bloodstains in Wusong and Zhabei are still fresh. The ladies and gentlemen of Shanghai have already resumed their extravagant and decadent lifestyle. Modern people are competing in swimming. As a result, artistic pictorials are filled with images of healthy and beautiful misses. Looking at the pictures, one can easily dissipate the spirit of warriors. However, the situation in the Northeast is urgent, and the land of Zhu has not been recovered. The Southern Ridge has fallen again, and the situation in Rehe is precarious. Do these modern people who bathe in water still dare to flaunt their sensuality in front of others when they occasionally think of the volunteer army shedding blood in the Northeast?

The plague is spreading, especially in the countryside. In Xihua Village in Guangfu Township, Suzhou, more than ten families in one village have lost more than twenty people. Although this is due to the close proximity of toilets and swarms of flies in the countryside, the prevalence of superstition is the main cause of death. According to local customs, when someone falls ill, they hire a witch and send away the plague god as the only effective way to cure the disease. The main offerings for sending away the plague god are half-cooked pig heads. After the god is sent away, they take it and devour it. Eating half-cooked meat surrounded by swarms of flies, even strong people can hardly avoid getting sick, let alone during a plague. The ignorance of the villagers is indeed laughable and pitiful. However, none of the first group of people who claim to transform the countryside have given any essential and practical lectures to the villagers on this serious issue. Instead, they focus on teaching the farmers a thousand-character text that can be read in three months, believing it to be the only essential tool for improving the countryside. This is truly regrettable.

A Night Sacrifice to Two Musicians by the Great Harmony Music Society (Part 1) 106

— Han

Mr. Zheng Jinwen of the Shanghai Great Harmony Music Society, in recent years, due to his advanced age, cherishes young music experts as if they were his own life. There is Wang Jihong, from Nantong, originally named Anxiang, who is skilled in the pipa and guqin, and personally taught by Mr. Zheng. There is also Liu Tianhua, from Jiangyin, whose skills are even more refined. He and Mr. Zheng are lifelong friends. Therefore, Mr. Zheng's expectations for the two are also very high. Now that the two have suddenly passed away one after another, the extent of Mr. Zheng's sorrow can be imagined. Therefore, he wrote a long parallel prose and, in the deep and quiet night of the twenty-second day of the seventh lunar month, sacrificed to the two alone in the music room of the Great Harmony Music Society. The article mentions the love triangle involving Jihong, in detail, which is precisely why he mourns him so deeply. As for Tianhua, he almost burst into tears. The text reads: "On the deep and quiet night of the twenty-second day of the seventh lunar month in the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, the old and clumsy Zheng Jinwen respectfully offers flowers, incense, wine, fruit, the Quanming qin, and the Guangling melody to the spirits of my disciples Wang Jihong and Liu Tianhua. Alas! Scholars die young, and talented people pass away early. Human misfortune is a common sorrow throughout the ages. Jihong and Tianhua are among them. Jihong studied poetry and books from a young age and was skilled in the arts. He did not change his original intentions due to the environment, nor did he alter his principles due to economic reasons. He was also an outstanding young man. In the eighth year of the Republic of China, Zhang Jian founded the Lingo School in Nantong and hired the drama scholar Ouyang Yuqian to be the principal. Jihong studied there. Later, the school was closed, and Jihong followed Yuqian to Shanghai. Yuqian, because he had plans to reorganize the New Stage, had no time to teach. So, he brought Jihong to the Great Harmony Music Society and said to me, 'This child can be taught.' He asked me to teach him in his place. I agreed. From then on, Jihong came every day. I asked him what he had learned. He said he was specializing in the pipa. I asked him to play. It was the legacy of the Haimen school. I disliked his moral character and asked him to fundamentally reform. I explained and demonstrated, and he was able to understand everything. In addition to the four-stringed pipa, he also studied the seven-stringed qin. His ambition became even stronger, and his skills improved day by day. He tuned to Midsummer, playing the dragon boats racing in the river. He played to Mid-Autumn, dancing to the phoenix leaves in the wind. The warm spring has feet, bringing the songs of birds and the fragrance of flowers. The white snow melts the cold, idly playing with the jade palaces in the sky. He was also a good material for national music and a strong figure in the art world. One day, he suddenly came to the society and told me, 'I recently composed the 'Full City Wind and Rain' melody and would like to have it corrected.' So, I played it once and asked for criticism. I said, 'The fingering and melody are flawless, but it only emphasizes the title. Wind, wind, rain, rain, rain, wind, there is no autumn heart of desolation, no autumn color of pessimism. It is a flaw.' However, what you just played is not easy to do. Jihong said, 'I am willing to be taught.' After a few days, he came again and said to me, 'The name Anxiang is too vulgar. I plan to change it to Qihong.' I strongly disagreed and said, 'The name does not need to be evil, but an ominous word cannot be used.' He then said, 'Then is it okay to use Jihong?' I said, 'It is better to use the two characters Jihong.' He seemed to agree. I immediately suspected that there was something different. Sure enough, I saw reports in various newspapers about two women marrying one man. For a time, it was spread as a good story. Some envied it, some admired it, and some were jealous of it. As for me, I was both happy and afraid. Happy because he had the double blessing of beauty, which must have been cultivated in a previous life. Afraid that a little yang energy would be exhausted.

Special Anti-Drug Publication

Full Text of Premier Sun's Anti-Drug Instruction 107

Premier Sun's anti-drug instruction, issued when he served as Grand Marshal in Guangzhou in the thirteenth year of the Republic of China, serves as a standard for those who advocate for the prohibition of opium. At a time when there is much debate, Premier Sun's instruction can truly serve as a compass for the authorities in charge of prohibition. It is specially published below:

In my opinion, the problem of opium prohibition in China is related to the problem of good government. The opium trade is absolutely incompatible with a national government endowed with the rights granted by the people. However, before the government authorities can implement measures to realize the authority of democracy, it is not possible to achieve effective prohibition. At present, illegal warlords not only encourage but also force the cultivation of opium within their jurisdictions. Elaborate and detailed plans for prohibition are of little use. This is because cultivating opium is simpler and more profitable than cultivating rice, vegetables, fruits, and other things. Therefore, most farmers are unwilling and dare not oppose the warlords' orders to force the cultivation of opium. The International League of Nations' anti-drug conference is about to open. The representatives of all countries attending the conference should uphold the spirit of fairness and resolutely establish strict plans to prohibit the production of opium and its derivatives (such as morphine, heroin, and other poisonous substances) in all countries. The result of the Chinese government's fragmentation has not only led to the resurgence of opium seedlings but also to the stagnation of foreign trade. Chinese and foreign merchants and manufacturers of legitimate goods have suffered huge losses. The huge amounts of money consumed by the smuggling and illegal sale of opium, if used for legitimate trade, would not only revitalize the country's commerce but also greatly improve legitimate trade between China and foreign countries. Recently, some have said that since opium has revived in our country today and poison is everywhere, it would be better to officially legalize the opium trade and allow foreign opium to be imported through customs to enrich the military expenditure. Such proposals are absolutely inappropriate. The public opinion of China, especially the law-abiding, peaceful, and pure people, is against opium. Anyone who advocates legalizing the opium trade or shows submission to the evil forces of opium, even if it is a temporary expedient, is a public enemy of the people. The current situation in the country is extremely bad, and the anti-drug movement is facing many difficulties, resulting in very little achievement. However, the declaration of war on opium must not be compromised or abandoned. If responsible government agencies, for their own private convenience and immediate benefit, lower the flag and cease fighting against opium, no matter how temporary, it is an act of treason. In short, any form of surrender to the scourge of opium can be said to be a disregard for the conscientious demands of the people. Even the bandit-like warlords who regard illegal opium as a source of profit dare not openly admit that they lack roads and convenient transportation facilities. In addition, there are frequent warlord struggles, which result in an increasing economic burden on farmers. Even if farmers want to peacefully cultivate ordinary agricultural products, it is impossible. For example, the Guangdong provincial government is extremely opposed to opium, but in addition to smuggling from neighboring provinces, foreign opium is also imported by sea. Under such circumstances, even if a good government like the Guangdong province braves all difficulties to crack down on the illegal opium trade and establish complete plans to fundamentally eliminate the poison, it is difficult to achieve substantial results due to the large number of smuggling activities by land and water. From this, we can see that local actions are difficult to achieve results. To achieve the goal of opium prohibition, the national government must adopt a national plan that is uniformly observed. Therefore, we should first defeat the warlords who are more deeply rooted and more harmful, promote the establishment of a national government, and enable it to realize the authority of democracy, so that opium prohibition can be effective. Today, the scourge that limits the people's lives and freedom, once abolished, will enable public opinion to achieve the goal of opium prohibition. At present, the warlords have not been defeated, and the democratic government has not yet unified the country. The best way to achieve the above-mentioned goals is for anti-drug groups to struggle unremittingly and continue to work on investigation and propaganda, so that illegal business has nowhere to hide. Even if it may not be effective for a time, we must never abandon the determination to persevere and not compromise. We should always adhere to a thorough and uncompromising policy.

Comrades:

Please fill in the pledge form and mail it along with your contact information to the Anti-Drug Association of the Republic of China at 4 Hong Kong Road, Shanghai, and you will receive a beautiful anti-drug publication (please enclose four cents for postage).

What Day is Today? Huang Jiahu 109

Today is the 90th anniversary of the Treaty of Nanjing and the opening day of the First National Anti-Drug Representative Assembly. When we recall Lin Zexu's spirit of eradicating opium and resisting strong enemies, he was eventually exiled due to the machinations of villains. Later, these mediocre and corrupt officials misled the country, resulting in the Treaty of Nanjing, ceding land and paying reparations, opening the door to the deadly poison that would destroy the country and exterminate the race, and planting the root of endless suffering. Thinking of this, I truly do not know where to find tears. The past is gone. What about now? Opium poppies are everywhere in the southwestern provinces. The authorities in Fujian and Anhui are driving people to plant opium. Yangtze River steamers, national railways, and private transportation of drugs are as frequent as weaving. Even national defense warships, amphibious aircraft, are inevitably caught carrying drugs from time to time. In the northern provinces, from the gentry and officials to the sedan carriers and runners, the addiction to white powder and red pills has spread throughout society. The special tax in Hubei and Hunan has not been abolished, and the public sale in Jiangsu is continuing. The central government's collection of opium tax has not been successfully realized. A disguised opium management agency has been officially approved to be established. Alas! The Northeast is gone. What about Rehe? The blood of Shanghai has not yet dried, and the situation in North China is again in danger. At this time when national disasters are looming, how should the whole country, from top to bottom, sharpen its will and strive to prepare for national salvation? Instead of doing this, we are eagerly committing suicide by indulging in drugs. Lin Wenzhong's efforts have all vanished. Premier Sun's instructions are shelved. The so-called party discipline and prohibition laws are also regarded as waste paper. How can the country not perish? My colleagues, seeing the rampant spread of opium and lamenting the imminent destruction of the race, are engaged in the anti-drug movement. We deeply feel the great responsibility and our own weak abilities. Therefore, we have convened the Eighth National Anti-Drug Representative Assembly, hoping to gather wisdom and benefit widely, and to unite our wills to form a stronghold, so that the anti-drug movement will become more and more sound and achieve the goal of eradicating opium. The opening day happens to be the anniversary of the Treaty of Nanjing, so as to show that we will not forget and encourage ourselves. I respectfully write a few words to preface this special publication.

The Mission of the National Anti-Drug Representative Assembly 110

The National Anti-Drug Representative Assembly will open in Shanghai today. What is its mission? I believe this is what the community wants to know. I will briefly describe it below.

Positive Aspects (1) To realize Premier Sun's Anti-Drug Instruction Everyone knows the harm of opium and drugs. For China, it is especially the reason for its weakness. Our nation, country, society, family, and international status are all declining. Tracing back to the beginning, which one is not caused by the harm of opium? Without opium, how could China be in this state today? Therefore, Premier Sun said, "The declaration of war on opium must not be compromised... Even if it may not be effective for a time, we must never abandon the determination to persevere and not compromise. We should always adhere to a thorough and uncompromising policy." Premier Sun's far-sightedness and deep understanding of our country's problems, and his firm advocacy of anti-drug policies, are rooted in his long-term concern for the country. His benevolent words are beneficial and widely applicable. Our people should sincerely regard them as a guideline, and persevere unremittingly, without changing or slackening, until success is achieved. At this National Anti-Drug Representative Assembly, the people, without any private agenda, dare not fail to inspire themselves and wage a life-and-death battle against opium and drugs, so as to live up to Premier Sun's spirit in heaven. (2) To unify the organization of the national anti-drug movement. In recent years, looking at the domestic anti-drug movement, although it has been severely damaged by the authorities in various places, its spirit has not been diminished. This is because right and wrong have not been obliterated, and justice is still in the hearts of the people. This humble sentiment, if it is appreciated by society, is because any widespread national movement, without a unified organization, is ultimately weak. As the ancients said, "A single tree is hard to support a mansion, but the will of the people can build a city." In the past, the national anti-drug movement was unable to act consistently due to the different environments in various places. Sympathizers deeply regretted it, and those who liked to stir up trouble criticized it. Therefore, this association plans to unify the organization of the national anti-drug movement, so that in the future, we can unite our strength and fight actively, easily achieving the effect of using arms and fingers together, without the worry of hesitating or diverging. (3) To formulate a strategy for fighting against the scourge of opium in the future. The scourge of opium is like a huge demon. Its evil influence is extensive and exceeds expectations. Our fight against it is like "the Tao is one foot high, but the demon is ten feet high." Therefore, this association plans to formulate a strategy for fighting against it in the future. Generally speaking, it will not go beyond the following three paths: (A) Striving to promote anti-drug education, so that it penetrates the hearts of the people, from children to adults, so that everyone is afraid of the harm of drugs and runs away from each other, without easily trying them. (B) Formulating a concrete opium prohibition plan, offering it to the central government, requesting its adoption, and promoting its realization from the perspective of the people. (C) Offering opium prohibition plans to officials in various places who have the sincerity to prohibit opium, and striving to help them realize them. The above three points, either starting from the lower level, so that the power of the drug demon will gradually diminish, or prompting politicians to advocate prohibition, so that the drug demon loses its support and is bound to gradually die out. We aim to achieve our goals, taking into account both overall planning, so that we can achieve twice the result with half the effort.

Negative Aspects Thoroughly oppose the public sale of opium and the opium business. The country has a prohibition law. Since our country claims to be a country ruled by law, we cannot ignore the law. The opium business, although profitable, is forbidden by morality and law. There is no doubt that if a private individual commits it, he will be imprisoned and despised by society. How much more so for those who hold the power of the country and rule the people? Although the calls for public sale have temporarily subsided, demons are lurking around, and trouble is brewing on all sides. There are many people who are eloquent and persuasive, trying to persuade the government to pursue drugs for profit. We should still be vigilant, consider all aspects, and not procrastinate or indulge, lest the government be unfortunately deceived, fall into the wrong path again, and make our anti-drug people unable to escape the deep condemnation of the people of the country. This is what this association hopes for from our anti-drug comrades at the beginning of the opening. As for the anti-drug issue, it is a major issue in China. The intelligence of the people in this association is short-sighted and shallow. We originally knew that we were not worthy of the great task, but a fool's idea may not be without a small contribution to the country. Gentlemen of the country, please teach us.

Dong Wenyuan on the Anti-Drug Movement of the Past Three Years 111

The National Anti-Drug Movement of the past three years has entered its most critical period. Seeing the rampant nature of the opium scourge and the laxity of prohibitions, we feel the immense weight of our responsibility. We have bravely risen up to fight against the evil forces. Surrounded by powerful enemies and facing all-round isolation, we have used only our bare hands to cry out loudly. How could our chances of success be anything more than a mantis trying to stop a chariot or throwing eggs against a rock? However, right and wrong have their own principles, and justice resides in the hearts of the people. We act on the dictates of our conscience, striving to save the country. Even though we make enemies of the powerful and incur the resentment of the influential, we have indeed gained the sympathy of public opinion and the support of the people, which is why we have been able to continue our existence and fight for the prohibition of opium. This is no accident. We hereby present a summary of the association's affairs over the past three years to inform fellow comrades and patriotic gentlemen who care about the anti-drug movement. We are grateful for the care and concern shown for the work of our association and hope for continued support to prevent it from being destroyed. If so, it would be fortunate for our country's opium prohibition, and not only for the anti-drug movement. In the past three years, the planting, transportation, sale, and consumption of opium in the country have not only not decreased but have instead shown a trend of increasing. Moreover, the import and spread of foreign narcotics is increasingly threatening to seize the opium market and replace it. The trend of injecting morphine is rampant in the three northeastern provinces, especially in the area around the South Manchuria Railway. In the provinces of North China along the Yellow River basin, the habit of smoking heroin has become widespread in the middle and lower classes. In the Yangtze River region and the southern provinces, opium smoking is still flourishing. However, the scourge of red pills in Jiangsu and Zhejiang is on the rise, with its poison spreading endlessly, which is truly heartbreaking. The southwestern provinces have always been opium-producing areas, and in recent years, the situation has worsened, even more so than before. Young students and ladies from prominent families are also often seen lying on opium couches, considering it nothing strange. General society even views smoking as being wealthy and being addicted as being fashionable. Local authorities in various provinces all regard protecting opium and forcing opium cultivation as their sole source of profit, inventing various pretexts and competing to follow suit. Farmers in Sichuan who do not grow opium are subjected to lazy donation fines, and villages in Fujian that refuse opium donations suffer the tragedy of being massacred. More recently, the Anhui Northern Anhui People's Uprising originated from opium taxes, and the Putian rebellion was also due to local taxes. Yangtze River steamboats and naval vessels that do not transport opium are as rare as morning stars. Airplanes transporting opium began in Guangdong and Yunnan, and soldiers in Fujian Province have also begun to imitate this. Since the beginning of this practice, the harm has become increasingly severe. Recently, even military advisors in the National Government have been found to carry opium. The Jiang'an steamboat incident involved another opium investigation. Furthermore, soldiers carrying opium are not allowed to be interfered with by police officers, and when high-ranking officials traffic drugs, the blame is often attributed to their attendants. Everyone from top to bottom is competing for profits, and the law is treated as mere empty words. To talk about opium prohibition is like seeking a tiger's skin. This is the general situation of the opium scourge within the country. As for the situation abroad, various international conferences have been convened, and investigation committees have traveled to East Asia, seemingly with a sincere intention to prohibit narcotics. In reality, however, each opium-benefiting country has ulterior motives, each aiming to protect their colonial opium tax revenue and domestic narcotic production. Therefore, the results have been nothing. The difficulties faced by the anti-drug movement under this internal and external aggression can be imagined.

Over these three years, the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association has remained true to its consistent policy, engaging in opium prohibition efforts without wavering or compromising. However, under these circumstances, the difficulties it has faced are beyond description, and the fact that work has not been able to proceed according to the original plan due to various obstacles is something that fellow comrades understand. Although the achievements of our association's work may not be entirely satisfactory, we have spared no effort and risked our lives in recent years. We dare not belittle or disregard the meager results we have achieved. We hereby present a general account and respectfully request review and guidance to benefit the future.

Resisting the public sale of opium has been the most important work of our association in the past three years. In just three years, the authorities have announced the implementation of public sales three times. The first public sale appeared in the spring of the 20th year of the Republic of China, promoted by Wu Liande, who utilized the gradual prohibition policy and was the head of the globally-renowned Opium Prohibition and Investigation Bureau. He gave it the beautiful name of "integrating prohibition with taxation," but in reality, it was simply tolerating drugs and collecting taxes. Our association, aware of the underlying schemes, made a clear announcement to the people of the country. At the same time, with clear banners, we expressed our thorough opposition to the authorities and urged the people of the country to wake up and resist in unison. Seeing that the general trend was not in their favor, the authorities' voices gradually subsided, and the first act of opposing public sale came to an end. Our association knew that the authorities' actions were not sincere and that a comeback was only a matter of time. Therefore, we remained vigilant and did not slacken, preparing for the greatest sacrifice to cope with the pressure and tragic actions of the authorities. As expected, the establishment of a narcotic management agency soon appeared in the newspapers. Our association persevered, vowing to never give up, sending telegrams and appeals like snowflakes. The authorities failed again. However, our association was exhausted and could no longer fight. After that, there was a period of relative quiet. The authorities temporarily lay dormant, waiting for an opportunity to act. Our association also took the opportunity to rest and conserve its strength. Between spring and summer of this year, the flames of public sale erupted again, spreading throughout the country, with an unprecedented level of rampant activity. The authorities were determined to go into the tiger's den, willing to sacrifice everything for this. Although our association faced dangers, we could not shirk our duty. Therefore, we generously intervened and fought to the death again, appealing to the people of the country and seeking assistance from neighboring countries. The authorities were eventually unable to continue, and the Executive Yuan reiterated opium prohibition and permanently abolished the evil system of public sale. This was originally official rhetoric and could not be easily believed. However, the Executive Yuan is a respected body, and it cannot be equated with the former. In addition, our association has also redoubled its efforts in investigation work. Previously, when the opium prohibition authorities intended to adopt the Taiwan opium public sale system, they sent Li Jihong to inspect it. Our association also sent Secretary-General Huang Jiawei to Taiwan to investigate. After returning, he compiled "A Glimpse of Opium Prohibition in Taiwan" and made it public to the people of the country. Second, we conducted a national survey of the drug situation, divided into regions and reaching the most remote areas, producing statistical tables. Last year, after the September 18th Incident in Shenyang, anti-Japanese propaganda surged throughout the country. Our association specifically compiled a memorandum summarizing the despicable behavior of the Japanese in China of spreading drugs to amass wealth and submitted it to the international investigation team to clarify the truth, and also announced the Nakamura Incident to dispel international doubts. Our association has spared no effort in supporting the overseas anti-drug movement. In addition to our association's Secretary-General Huang personally going to various colonial territories in Southeast Asia to promote the anti-drug movement and advocate for the organization of anti-drug groups the year before, last autumn, our association sent Education Committee member Chen Xixiang to Singapore to assist in establishing the Singapore Anti-Drug Association and went to various places to promote it vigorously. The results were very good. Those that have been established include the Singapore and Batavia Anti-Drug Associations, and the rest are still in preparation. The opium scourge in Fujian and Anhui has caused several major waves, which are deeply entrenched and difficult to reverse. Because soldiers were protecting it and officials were colluding with each other, local anti-drug groups vowed to fight to the death, but achieved little effect. Our association, feeling its responsibility, could not bear to avoid it. Therefore, we resisted unanimously, vowing to share the same hatred, with frequent correspondence and telegrams reaching hundreds of pages. However, warlords and corrupt officials resorted to delaying tactics, continuing their actions in secret, causing the opium scourge in Fujian and Anhui to remain severe to this day. This is the most heartbreaking thing for our association, and we can only sigh in vain. Our association is a people's organization with no resources for production. What it relies on to maintain itself is a small amount of funds for support. Now, as these funds are exhausted, we have repeatedly tried to raise donations, but all efforts have been sabotaged by the enemy and have not been fully successful. The enemy has a strong latent power, resorting to suppression and intimidation. Not only are those who are powerless unable to help, but even those who are enthusiastic and wealthy are afraid of trouble and dare not donate. This kind of poisonous scheme is enough to control the lifeline of our association. However, our association has not been discouraged by this and continues to run around with endless hope, still planning to build a Lin Zexu Memorial Hall when the environment is more favorable, as a model for future generations in anti-drug efforts. We are now actively handling the preparatory procedures and will implement it as soon as the economy shows a slight improvement. At the same time, we will continue to hold a more magnificent national anti-drug tour, so that the concept of anti-drug efforts penetrates the center of society. Although our association's wishes are extravagant, with the sympathy and assistance of the people of the country, what we are doing will be very easy.

[P National Anti-Drug Conference Opens Tonight

Over a Hundred Registered Delegates

Banquet at the China Society at 7 PM Tonight

The National Anti-Drug Delegates Conference, which has been widely publicized, is scheduled to hold its opening ceremony at 7 PM tonight at the China Society, 150 Weihai Road. Chinese National Anti-Drug Association Chairman Wang Jingqi, Vice-Chairman Li Denghui, and Secretary-General Huang Jiawei will jointly host a banquet for all the delegates. The program includes the chairman announcing the mission of the National Conference, the director of the conference preparatory committee reporting on the preparatory process, followed by reports from delegates from various provinces and overseas on the opium prohibition and opium scourge situation in their respective regions, speeches by guests, and other items. United China Film Company will also be on-site to film the conference newsreel. The conference's business meeting is scheduled to be held at 9 AM tomorrow at the same location. It is reported that as of last night, more than 140 delegates had arrived, with more than 80 proposals submitted. Various organizational groups in the city have also sent delegates. It is reported that due to the limited space at the venue, the association is unable to accommodate representatives from non-organizational groups, for which they express their apologies. As for the unofficial delegates who had previously requested to participate, they will be placed in the guest seats for accommodation. Delegates from other cities and representatives from local organizations who have not yet registered are requested to contact the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association at 4 Hong Kong Road before 4 PM today in order to be included in the seating arrangement at the venue.

How can they then seek to serve the country? I am unable to serve due to illness. How is this different from a traitor serving the country? Telegram from the Geneva International Anti-Drug News Agency 113

To Mr. Jiawei: We have learned that your association will hold a National Delegates Conference to discuss future anti-drug issues. I humbly offer a few of my views, hoping you will consider them: (1) Firmly request the government to abide by the articles of the International Opium Conference in Geneva on February 19, 1925, and the International Conference on the Limitation of the Manufacture of Narcotic Drugs in Geneva on July 13, 1931. (2) Firmly request the government to ask the Advisory Committee on Traffic in Opium and Other Dangerous Drugs of the League of Nations to investigate the opium scourge in various concessions or leased territories in China, and request the governments of countries with concessions or leased territories in China to provide a detailed report on the drug situation in each concession. As for the drug situation in the Shanghai International Settlement, the appropriate authorities can be held responsible for reporting it. (3) Sincerely cooperate with the League of Nations and submit detailed annual reports to the League of Nations, because although the Chinese government has annual reports submitted to the League of Nations, there may be shortcomings regarding the opium issue for certain reasons. (4) Publish an annual report on opium and drugs in China, especially detailing the smuggling of drugs by foreign ships and the harm they cause to China. (5) Publish a special edition on opium and narcotic drug issues annually in prominent foreign newspapers in China (such as the opium special edition of the Peking and Tientsin Times in 1919 and 1920). The above points, in my opinion, may be beneficial if they can be discussed at the Delegates Conference. I hope for the best. I wish you well. Browne, President of the Geneva International Anti-Drug News Agency.

Resolution of the Executive Committee of the Women's International League for Peace and Freedom, British Section 115

(1) The Opium Committee of the Women's International League for Peace and Freedom strongly supports the assertion of the Far East Opium Investigation Team that "opium should not be regarded as a legitimate commodity, and all opium needs, except for medical and scientific needs, should be regarded as illegal." (2) We firmly believe that government public sales of smoking opium are clearly in violation of Article 6 of the Geneva International Opium Conference, and that our (British) failure to fulfill international obligations in colonies and dependencies damages our national honor and endangers the friendship between China and Britain. (3) We also hope that the recommendations of the investigation team, (A) to limit the amount of opium smoked by addicts through a registration method in order to achieve the goal of prohibition, and (B) to abolish the inclusion of opium revenue in the tax revenue budget, will be immediately implemented in Britain and the Far East.

Opium Problems That Triggered the Manchurian Incident 121

Written by Kikuchi Yuji, Executive Secretary of the Japan Opium Poisoning Prevention Association. Following the Manchurian Incident, the Shanghai War erupted again. These two major incidents have made countries worldwide feel uneasy about the prospects for peace and have brought the League of Nations peace efforts to a standstill. What are the true reasons for these two cases? This is something we must study. To enable all countries to understand the truth about the Far East conflict and clarify where the entanglement lies, it is necessary to start with the relationship between the opium problem and the two cases.

The reason for the Manchurian Incident claimed by our Japanese military is that Chinese soldiers destroyed our railways and attacked our garrison troops. Therefore, we had no choice but to exercise our right of self-defense and occupy key points in Manchuria. Can the words of soldiers be believed? Anyone with a conscience in the world must investigate the facts and their rights and wrongs. Standing on the grounds of humanity and justice, we must carefully examine the root causes and truths. People of all countries must work together to study right and wrong, break evil and promote righteousness. This is the right way to maintain world peace and create happiness for mankind.

If we blindly follow the actions of reckless people and mislead the country's future, or allow their rampant aggression without the people coming out to stop them, it will plunge the country into a crisis from which it cannot save itself. The result will inevitably lead to the most tragic Far East war. The most dangerous thing is forgetting the spirit of international cooperation and the unrestrained ambitions of the military and political authorities who want to force their way. Our people should bear full responsibility for the reckless actions of these people, and few of our people know their illegality and want to correct them. Now, we are still allowing warlords to overstep their bounds, which can be said to be proof of our people's lack of self-awareness.

I believe that the opium and narcotic drug problem will inevitably lead to major international disputes in the future from a humanitarian perspective. Since I regretted it early on and stopped doing morphine business, I gathered fellow traders who were doing opium and morphine business in China, abolished this harmful business, and organized groups to prevent drug poisoning until today. Three months before the Liaoning Incident, my comrades knew in advance that a major incident would occur in the near future due to the opium problem. Sure enough, on the night of September 18th of the previous year, the Japanese army occupied Shenyang and Jilin. At present, the Japanese people and the military involved seem to have forgotten the cause, or deliberately concealed the true cause from mankind to obscure world opinion. However, what made the Japanese army so excited and determined to destroy the world as a cause is a big mistake. The real cause is the Japanese people's secret sale of opium and morphine drugs. The Japanese people's drug sales have often been the seeds of Sino-Japanese disputes. The beginning of the Liaoning Incident originated from Zhang Ji's speech in February 1931. Zhang said, "The Japanese army in major cities in China is protecting Japanese people's conspiracy of opium, morphine, and other drugs, which are poisoning China." The Japanese military believed that this statement was a criticism of the Japanese army's reputation. The Japanese embassy requested Zhang Ji to withdraw his previous statement and swear to the Japanese government that he would not mention this matter again. Zhang Ji ignored it and instead listed facts to refute the Japanese military's request. The Japanese military became angry and turned its sharp edge to attack the Japanese Foreign Ministry for being weak and incompetent, believing that the matter concerned the credibility of the Japanese army and wanted to resolve it by force.

At that time, the arrival of an American pilot in Japan caused a major international problem. The newspapers had no space to take care of the military's face, and the world missed the opportunity to investigate the drug sales problem. In late June, the Captain Nakamura incident and the Wanbaoshan incident followed. The Japanese military was overjoyed and excited, saying that the opportunity for revenge had arrived. The Japanese military then misled Japan's century-long plan for the current excitement. The military's attitude can also be said to be a method of using any means to achieve its goals. However, can its fault be entirely attributed to the Japanese army? Zhang Ji's method of accusing is also not without its shortcomings. I have a lot of information about Zhang's inappropriateness, but the purpose of this article is not here. There is no need to say that the purpose of this discussion is to clarify that the Japanese people's doing improper business has a great impact on the future of world peace. For the sake of human happiness, what kind of determination should the Japanese people who do improper business make? This is the main purpose of this article.

The matters listed by Zhang Ji are all facts, and we are ashamed of our compatriots. However, there are various reasons why Japanese people do this kind of business. One is the geographical convenience, the short travel time, and the convenient transportation, which makes it easy to smuggle in. The second is the economic benefit, with little labor and high income, making it easy to get rich. This is the fundamental reason why many Japanese people do this kind of business. This has caused continuous Sino-Japanese disputes. I deeply hope that people of good will in the world will pay attention to this matter and work together to study and remedy the situation, so as to avoid eternal conflict between the Chinese and Japanese people.

The reasons why Japanese people tend to this kind of bad habit are worth studying. In my opinion, after Japan's victory in the Russo-Japanese War, more and more Japanese people went to Manchuria to make a living. They all contacted the Chinese with the prestige of the victors, but they were not as hardworking and thrifty as the Chinese in managing their families. The victor in the war became the loser in the economy. They could not compete with the Chinese in business. Japanese people with small capital wanted to find a shortcut to get rich, and finally became obsessed with the improper business of opium and morphine. This became a common practice. China's opium prohibition has been a national policy to this day. Because of political disrepair, the more opium is prohibited, the more opium addicts there are. In 1911, the Sino-British Opium Agreement was established, prohibiting the import of Indian opium. Strict prohibition policies were also implemented domestically. After the Qing Dynasty fell, the provinces were occupied by warlords, and internal strife continued. They each sought their own interests, and the opium prohibition order had become a mere piece of paper. Under the surrounding of this environment and the real situation in China, foreigners gradually increased in major cities in China, and opium and morphine spread throughout the cities. Among them, due to the geographical proximity, many Japanese people came to China, so most of those who engaged in this business were also Japanese. This is inevitable.

The trade of drugs such as opium and morphine is mostly concentrated in Dalian, Shanghai, and Kobe. From these three ports, they are transshipped to Tianjin, Qingdao, Shenyang, Jinan, and other places. Japanese people do improper business in these places, and Japanese officials also have the intention to crack down and control them, but for the sake of overseas development of their own people, they are not very strict. This is the reason why many Japanese people do this improper business. There are also many people from European and American countries who do this business in China, and the amount of their transactions is far above that of the Japanese. Because there are not many of them, they have less chance of attracting the attention of the Chinese. The reason why Japanese people attract the attention of the Chinese is because there are many of them and their numbers are small.

The Chinese are old customers of drugs, and there are also reasons for this. China has been in internal turmoil for many years, the economy is exhausted, the politics are not repaired, and the opium prohibition system is destroyed by warlords. Opium prohibition has become opium, and opium profits are used for military expenses and warlord profits. In addition, after the European war, too many narcotic drugs produced in Europe flowed into China, and the amount was very large. Moreover, warlords forced people to cut poppies everywhere, so the harm of opium spread throughout the country. The tragic situation cannot be exhausted by pen and paper. In a certain village in North China, 48% of the people are addicted to narcotics. Half of the reason is the corruption of the Chinese government's rule, and the other half must be attributed to the crime of the Japanese sellers. The Japanese people must understand the sins committed by their compatriots in China and share their responsibilities together.

Chinese people observe this kind of fact, and many newspaper reporters and groups believe that the Japanese government is manipulating and assisting behind the scenes, or that the Japanese army is protecting behind the scenes with the intention of exterminating the Chinese people. They use various methods and means to fight against Japan, awaken the people's reflection, and expect the development of the nation, which can also be said to be a matter of course. However, a certain big country, the culprit of China's drug abuse, wants to permanently suppress China with imperialist methods, which can be said to be no less than Japan. From the observation of historical facts, a certain big country must be responsible for the creation of international disputes with the opium problem as the center. Among the nationalists in Japan, there is a group of people who believe that the Chinese people's national character is superior to that of the Japanese people, and they may not be able to defeat the Chinese people in the future. Therefore, they must use the opium policy to poison the Chinese people and maintain the superior position of the Japanese people. Their shortsightedness is beyond reach. In the concessions, there are many opium dens and narcotic drug stores. The luggage inspection of the troops stationed in China is very lenient on the inspection of such drugs, which can also prove the intention of the imperialists. There are many disputes between the two countries that have occurred after this kind of practical problem, and the number is countless. The Jinan Incident is closely related to the opium problem. The Japanese government explained the reason for the Jinan Incident, that the Northern Expeditionary Army abused and killed people, and the Japanese army came to protect the overseas Chinese. However, our country has long known that the real reason is still the opium problem. The reason why the Chinese army hates the Japanese is the grudges that have been accumulated over the years. Killing the Japanese is just the result. Japanese overseas Chinese have been using opium and morphine to make profits and deeply poison the Chinese people for several years. Therefore, several major negotiations have occurred between China and Japan. The Japanese people's drug trafficking is often reported by Chinese newspapers. The people hate the Japanese people's drug trafficking, so the Chinese army killed the Japanese drug traffickers, and the Japanese army protected the improper Japanese people. This is the truth of the Jinan Incident. The cause of the Jinan Incident is also the cause of the Beian Incident. However, the people of the two countries, especially the Japanese military, have forgotten the true cause. It is enough to make people reflect on causing international disputes due to such inhuman behavior. Why repeat the disaster again and again?

The Jinan Incident caused a major problem at the International League of Nations Opium Conference (January 1929). At that time, Dr. Wang Jingqi, the Chinese representative, had a section in his statement discussing the relationship between the Jinan Incident and the opium problem. The content said that the Japanese army's dispatch to Shandong and the Japanese army in China strongly supported Japanese merchants selling opium and morphine. Therefore, it is very difficult for China to crack down on opium. Regarding this statement, the Japanese representative, Committee Member Sato, was very angry and retorted that the Chinese committee member's words made people around the world feel that the Japanese army was related to the opium problem. The Japanese army has never been criticized by outsiders in terms of discipline. For the reputation of the Japanese army, this statement cannot be taken lightly. This kind of debate was published in Chinese newspapers. Later, the Chinese people started an anti-Japanese trend again, which had a very deep impression on the Chinese people. Soon, a major opium smuggling case occurred in Japan. Those involved were people from the political circles. The so-called Abe Yoshiya incident. The people who were impeached were Prime Minister Tanaka, Minister Kuhara, and Commander of the Yamaguchi Near Guard Division. The Commander of the Yamaguchi Division resigned as a result. When this news reached China, the Chinese people became more convinced that the Japanese military supported the Japanese people's drug trafficking. As a result, the relationship between the two countries, China and Japan, increased, and the overall situation in the Far East gradually became eventful.

The accumulation of such facts led to Zhang Ji's accusation against the Japanese military. However, the opium problem is not only a major humanitarian problem, but also a major international problem. The treaties made for the opium problem have mostly become waste paper. The problem of banning opium and narcotic drugs, which is of great significance to human health, is now a tool for disturbing peace in the Far East. Regarding this problem, the people of China and Japan must reflect deeply and appeal to the whole world. For the sake of human happiness, we must seek a perfect solution, then the purpose of this article will be achieved.
